Coldspring. I'm sure the well-known couple that were first aboard
will get some interesting passengers to ride with.

Texas Tour Bus 2

From: Baileys Bunch (baileys_bunch@yahoo.com) | Date: 2007-01-21 22:08:10 UTC
Howdy Ya'll
It's rodeo time in Houston and the cow-poke that just got on the bus
needs to get "Strait" to Reliant Stadium.
The bus driver has parked the bus on far from the "Rodeo Rest Stop" to
pick-up more passengers and to continue on his route.
17 paces Eastward from the Rodeo Rest Stop to a fallen tree running
parallel to the ravine,laying between this fallen tree and a medium
pine tree, X marks the spot for pick-up.

Happy Trails,
Bailey's Bunch




Texas Tour Bus 2

From: dewberrylb (dewberrylb@gmail.com) | Date: 2007-02-19 18:54:22 UTC
Funny Kim should ask about the tour buses. I have been trying to get
#2, but kept finding people parked right near where I needed to be.
This mission took on a greater urgency because this upcoming weekend
is trailrider weekend--the horses and riders will all be camping out
in Memorial Park. So, this morning, before cars were allowed access
to the picnic loop, I walked over to the spot and picked up the bus.

Here's info on the trailrides:
http://www.rodeohouston.com/wh/wh_tr.aspx

We usually hang out on Memorial Saturday morning to watch the trail
riders as they leave the park on their way to the downtown parade. We
won't be able to do that this weekend, so we'll try to catch them as
they come into town on Friday.

While I was at Memorial Park, I checked on my own Rodeo Rest Stop
(soon to enjoy its third trailrider campout) and Alien Logic. Alien
Logic is there, but its bonus box is missing. I'll try to replace it
at some point, but I have some other letterboxing projects higher on
the list. I also found a newly planted geocache (without GPS), so it
was a fun morning.

dewberry


Re: [letterboxingtexas] Texas Tour Bus 2

From: (kacmbc@aol.com) | Date: 2007-02-19 15:09:34 UTC-05:00
As a side note to watching the trail riders arrive in Memorial Park, don't forget about the Rodeo Parade downtown Saturday morning!  The parade starts at 10:00 and is preceded at 9:50 by the Conoco Phillips Rodeo Run 5K and 10K!  Runners get to run along the parade route prior to all of the horses!  BONUS!!!
 
See y'all out there!!!
 
Runs for Chocolate  :)

Texas Tour Bus 2

From: maryjo_rekedal (mjrekedal@gmail.com) | Date: 2008-01-10 03:49:45 UTC
Fellow Texas Boxers,

The Texas Tour Bus 2 is back on the road. The passengers spent a
quiet Christmas in Austin, and even took time to help me move my
elderly parents into independent living. (We needed the bus to load
boxes and the people on the bus to carry boxes and furniture into the
new place. Not one passenger uttered a word of complaint!)

But everyone is back on the bus, with one additional traveler. When
last seen, the bus was in Bosque County, stopping to visit the
cemetery of Our Savior's Lutheran Church in Norse.

Don't bother looking at Mapquest for the directions to Norse. They
have it situated east of Clifton, when all locals know that Norse is
west of Clifton.

Going north on I-35 from Austin area, exit Temple and take Hwy 36
west to Gatesville. Continue on 36 for 6 miles to 182. Turn right on
182 for 20 miles thru Turnersville to intersection with Hwy 219, the
Cleng Peerson Memorial Hwy. Cross 219, jogging right and left,
continue on 182 for 2.2 miles to Our Savior's Lutheran Church.

If you are coming from the north, travel south on I-35 to Waco, then
take Hwy 6 west to Clifton. (Stop for a piece of scrumptious pie at
the Tea House on the corner of Ave D and 5th St.) From Hwy 6 turn
left on Hwy 219, Cleng Peerson Memorial Hwy. Drive 6.9 miles to 182.
Turn right on 182, traveling 2.2 miles to Our Savior's Luther Church.

Park on the right by the entrace gate to the cemetery. Notice the
monument to the first 17 Norwegians to settle in Bosque Cnty. Once
inside the cemetery, locate the prominent grave marker of Cleng
Peerson. Pay him tribute. Then continue straight ahead to the rock
wall. Locate the grave of Martha Louise and her infant child.
Directly opposite her grave stone is a cedar tree behind the wall.
The tour bus is perched on a ledge behind the wall, under those cedar
branches.

Happy touring!
Bloomin' Gramma Jo and Bird Dog

Texas Tour Bus 2

From: iraboxer (iraboxer@yahoo.com) | Date: 2008-08-07 19:36:54 UTC
Being a ghost sometimes has its perks; you can meet and chat with
other ghosts, some of whom were famous and important mortals. Just
the other day I was thinking about Davy Crockett and wondering what
was up with him, so I took a little trip over to the Alamo and found
him (more properly, his ghost), sitting there looking a little
dejected. He was still wearing his old buckskins and that coonskin
cap which was getting a little scraggly looking, if you ask me, and
he was cleaning his old Tennessee long rifle. Anyway, I asked him
how he had been doing and he allowed as to how he was doin' tol'able,
except that he missed his favorite pastime, which was hunting and
asked if I knew if there were any bears around, any old kind would
do. I told him that there were very few bears left in Texas because
people like him had killed them all. He said he was sorry about that
and would like to make amends if he could. Maybe he could find a
bear, just any old bear, and apologize for killing so many of them in
his lifetime. I told him that I knew of a bear out west of Houston,
but that he was just a Baby Bear. I asked him if he would like to
take a trip on the Texas Tour Bus and I'd show him where the cub
lived, if he would promise that he only wanted to apologize. He
brightened up at the prospect and said he'd just take me up on it.
We got on board with all the other well-known Texans, a few of whom
he remembered, and some he had heard of, and headed for a place
called Cypress, where I knew the little bear lived. Pretty soon,
Davy (or more properly, his ghost), took over the wheel and drove
that bus all the way to Cypress. I don't know how he learned to
drive, but ghosts can do about anything they want to if they try hard
enough. We found the house of the Baby Bear and he parked out front,
surveying the neighborhood, which was a very nice one, indeed, for a
Baby Bear. Then, he turned up the walk and, just before he got to
the front door, he thought he heard something, so he turned to the
right and ducked under some bushes. The last I saw of him, he was
sitting on top of the bus sighting in that long rifle, with a grin on
his face and a gleam in his eye. I have no idea what he had in mind.

The Ghost of IRA Boxer

> how he had been doing and he allowed as to how he was doin'
tol'able,
> except that he missed his favorite pastime, which was hunting and
> asked if I knew if there were any bears around, any old kind would
> do. I told him that there were very few bears left in Texas
because
> people like him had killed them all. He said he was sorry about
that
> and would like to make amends if he could. Maybe he could find a
> bear, just any old bear, and apologize for killing so many of them
in
> his lifetime. I told him that I knew of a bear out west of
Houston,
> but that he was just a Baby Bear. I asked him if he would like to
> take a trip on the Texas Tour Bus and I'd show him where the cub
> lived, if he would promise that he only wanted to apologize. He
> brightened up at the prospect and said he'd just take me up on it.
> We got on board with all the other well-known Texans, a few of whom
> he remembered, and some he had heard of, and headed for a place
> called Cypress, where I knew the little bear lived. Pretty soon,
> Davy (or more properly, his ghost), took over the wheel and drove
> that bus all the way to Cypress. I don't know how he learned to
> drive, but ghosts can do about anything they want to if they try
hard
> enough. We found the house of the Baby Bear and he parked out
front,
> surveying the neighborhood, which was a very nice one, indeed, for
a
> Baby Bear. Then, he turned up the walk and, just before he got to
> the front door, he thought he heard something, so he turned to the
> right and ducked under some bushes. The last I saw of him, he was
> sitting on top of the bus sighting in that long rifle, with a grin
on
> his face and a gleam in his eye. I have no idea what he had in
mind.
>
> The Ghost of IRA Boxer
>

Re: [letterboxingtexas] Texas Tour Bus 2

From: janet clark (jayceeinbedford@yahoo.com) | Date: 2008-08-07 21:04:47 UTC-07:00
Awesome, totally awesome!
 
Janet
iraboxer <iraboxer@yahoo.com> wrote:
Being a ghost sometimes has its perks; you can meet and chat with
other ghosts, some of whom were famous and important mortals. Just
the other day I was thinking about Davy Crockett and wondering what
was up with him, so I took a little trip over to the Alamo and found
him (more properly, his ghost), sitting there looking a little
dejected. He was still wearing his old buckskins and that coonskin
cap which was getting a little scraggly looking, if you ask me, and
he was cleaning his old Tennessee long rifle. Anyway, I asked him
how he had been doing and he allowed as to how he was doin' tol'able,
except that he missed his favorite pastime, which was hunting and
asked if I knew if there were any bears around, any old kind would
do. I told him that there were very few bears left in Texas because
people like him had killed them all. He said he was sorry about that
and would like to make amends if he could. Maybe he could find a
bear, just any old bear, and apologize for killing so many of them in
his lifetime. I told him that I knew of a bear out west of Houston,
but that he was just a Baby Bear. I asked him if he would like to
take a trip on the Texas Tour Bus and I'd show him where the cub
lived, if he would promise that he only wanted to apologize. He
brightened up at the prospect and said he'd just take me up on it.
We got on board with all the other well-known Texans, a few of whom
he remembered, and some he had heard of, and headed for a place
called Cypress, where I knew the little bear lived. Pretty soon,
Davy (or more properly, his ghost), took over the wheel and drove
that bus all the way to Cypress. I don't know how he learned to
drive, but ghosts can do about anything they want to if they try hard
enough. We found the house of the Baby Bear and he parked out front,
surveying the neighborhood, which was a very nice one, indeed, for a
Baby Bear. Then, he turned up the walk and, just before he got to
the front door, he thought he heard something, so he turned to the
right and ducked under some bushes. The last I saw of him, he was
sitting on top of the bus sighting in that long rifle, with a grin on
his face and a gleam in his eye. I have no idea what he had in mind.

The Ghost of IRA Boxer

From: Maribeth Jagger (cjagger405@earthlink.net) | Date: 2008-08-08 02:01:34 UTC-05:00

I quietly spent my afternoon checking on one of my letterboxing in Tioga, Texas - birthplace of Gene Autry, the singing cowboy for goodness sake. What could be a more wholesome activity? Then after preparing a lovely dinner and washing the dishes by hand, I sat meekly in my chair, knitting and listening to classical music. All this talk of my attempting to steal that lovely box from that dear young bear is... well... is just slanderous. I may have to have a word with Mother of All Those Many Children for offering my name up in the first place. Whadda ya say, Mo5, wanna meet me for a Shiner in Buffalo, I mean, an iced beverage in some quiet place? Maybe you could bring along your barefoot friend and I could counsel her on all that name calling... Puddle Bozo, indeed! Now I must go attend to my ironing and can some peaches.
Sincerely,
Puddle Splasher

--- In letterboxingtexas@yahoogroups.com, "iraboxer" <iraboxer@...>
wrote:
>
> Being a ghost sometimes has its perks; you can meet and chat with
> other ghosts, some of whom were famous and important mortals. Just
> the other day I was thinking about Davy Crockett and wondering what
> was up with him, so I took a little trip over to the Alamo and
found
> him (more properly, his ghost), sitting there looking a little
> dejected. He was still wearing his old buckskins and that coonskin
> cap which was getting a little scraggly looking, if you ask me, and
> he was cleaning his old Tennessee long rifle. Anyway, I asked him
> how he had been doing and he allowed as to how he was doin'
tol'able,
> except that he missed his favorite pastime, which was hunting and
> asked if I knew if there were any bears around, any old kind would
> do. I told him that there were very few bears left in Texas
because
> people like him had killed them all. He said he was sorry about
that
> and would like to make amends if he could. Maybe he could find a
> bear, just any old bear, and apologize for killing so many of them
in
> his lifetime. I told him that I knew of a bear out west of
Houston,
> but that he was just a Baby Bear. I asked him if he would like to
> take a trip on the Texas Tour Bus and I'd show him where the cub
> lived, if he would promise that he only wanted to apologize. He
> brightened up at the prospect and said he'd just take me up on it.
> We got on board with all the other well-known Texans, a few of whom
> he remembered, and some he had heard of, and headed for a place
> called Cypress, where I knew the little bear lived. Pretty soon,
> Davy (or more properly, his ghost), took over the wheel and drove
> that bus all the way to Cypress. I don't know how he learned to
> drive, but ghosts can do about anything they want to if they try
hard
> enough. We found the house of the Baby Bear and he parked out
front,
> surveying the neighborhood, which was a very nice one, indeed, for
a
> Baby Bear. Then, he turned up the walk and, just before he got to
> the front door, he thought he heard something, so he turned to the
> right and ducked under some bushes. The last I saw of him, he was
> sitting on top of the bus sighting in that long rifle, with a grin
on
> his face and a gleam in his eye. I have no idea what he had in
mind.
>
> The Ghost of IRA Boxer
>




--
Barefoot Lucy
"It's not about footwear, it's about philosophy"

Now isn't it odd that when Viewfinder and I would play "cowboys" as kids, instead of wanting to be Gene Autry or Roy Rogers, I always chose to be Billy the Kid? Of course she was always the beautiful school marm. It was a lot of fun until in my over-zealousness, I decided to rob her once, and she ended up with laying on the sofa with an ice pack on her head, and our mother had taken away my "six shooter" and told me hitting my sister on the head with it was not appropriate. Well, Lucy, what can I say? Once a thief, always a thief, and now I've got my sights set on that TTB. (My mother returned my six shooter long ago, but I'll need to find some caps for it.)
Puddle Splasher

--- In letterboxingtexas@yahoogroups.com, "iraboxer" <iraboxer@...>

wrote:
>
> Being a ghost sometimes has its perks; you can meet and chat with
> other ghosts, some of whom were famous and important mortals. Just
> the other day I was thinking about Davy Crockett and wondering what
> was up with him, so I took a little trip over to the Alamo and
found
> him (more properly, his ghost), sitting there looking a little
> dejected. He was still wearing his old buckskins and that coonskin
> cap which was getting a little scraggly looking, if you ask me, and
> he was cleaning his old Tennessee long rifle. Anyway, I asked him
> how he had been doing and he allowed as to how he was doin'
tol'able,
> except that he missed his favorite pastime, which was hunting and
> asked if I knew if there were any bears around, any old kind would
> do. I told him that there were very few bears left in Texas
because
> people like him had killed them all. He said he was sorry about
that
> and would like to make amends if he could. Maybe he could find a
> bear, just any old bear, and apologize for killing so many of them
in
> his lifetime. I told him that I knew of a bear out west of
Houston,
> but that he was just a Baby Bear. I asked him if he would like to
> take a trip on the Texas Tour Bus and I'd show him where the cub
> lived, if he would promise that he only wanted to apologize. He
> brightened up at the prospect and said he'd just take me up on it.
> We got on board with all the other well-known Texans, a few of whom
> he remembered, and some he had heard of, and headed for a place
> called Cypress, where I knew the little bear lived. Pretty soon,
> Davy (or more properly, his ghost), took over the wheel and drove
> that bus all the way to Cypress. I don't know how he learned to
> drive, but ghosts can do about anything they want to if they try
hard
> enough. We found the house of the Baby Bear and he parked out
front,
> surveying the neighborhood, which was a very nice one, indeed, for
a
> Baby Bear. Then, he turned up the walk and, just before he got to
> the front door, he thought he heard something, so he turned to the
> right and ducked under some bushes. The last I saw of him, he was
> sitting on top of the bus sighting in that long rifle, with a grin
on
> his face and a gleam in his eye. I have no idea what he had in
mind.
>
> The Ghost of IRA Boxer
>

On 8/8/08, Maribeth Jagger <cjagger405@earthlink.net> wrote:

I am soooo innocent. My character has been defamed - unjustly accused. I quietly spent my afternoon checking on one of my letterboxing in Tioga, Texas - birthplace of Gene Autry, the singing cowboy for goodness sake. What could be a more wholesome activity? Then after preparing a lovely dinner and washing the dishes by hand, I sat meekly in my chair, knitting and listening to classical music. All this talk of my attempting to steal that lovely box from that dear young bear is... well... is just slanderous. I may have to have a word with Mother of All Those Many Children for offering my name up in the first place. Whadda ya say, Mo5, wanna meet me for a Shiner in Buffalo, I mean, an iced beverage in some quiet place? Sincerely,
Puddle Splasher

I am soooo innocent. My character has been defamed - unjustly accused. I quietly spent my afternoon checking on one of my letterboxing in Tioga, Texas - birthplace of Gene Autry, the singing cowboy for goodness sake. What could be a more wholesome activity? --- In letterboxingtexas@yahoogroups.com, "iraboxer" <iraboxer@...>

wrote:
>
> Being a ghost sometimes has its perks; you can meet and chat with
> other ghosts, some of whom were famous and important mortals. Just
> the other day I was thinking about Davy Crockett and wondering what
> was up with him, so I took a little trip over to the Alamo and
found
> him (more properly, his ghost), sitting there looking a little
> dejected. He was still wearing his old buckskins and that coonskin
> cap which was getting a little scraggly looking, if you ask me, and
> he was cleaning his old Tennessee long rifle. Anyway, I asked him
> how he had been doing and he allowed as to how he was doin'
tol'able,
> except that he missed his favorite pastime, which was hunting and
> asked if I knew if there were any bears around, any old kind would
> do. I told him that there were very few bears left in Texas
because
> people like him had killed them all. He said he was sorry about
that
> and would like to make amends if he could. Maybe he could find a
> bear, just any old bear, and apologize for killing so many of them
in
> his lifetime. I told him that I knew of a bear out west of
Houston,
> but that he was just a Baby Bear. I asked him if he would like to
> take a trip on the Texas Tour Bus and I'd show him where the cub
> lived, if he would promise that he only wanted to apologize. He
> brightened up at the prospect and said he'd just take me up on it.
> We got on board with all the other well-known Texans, a few of whom
> he remembered, and some he had heard of, and headed for a place
> called Cypress, where I knew the little bear lived. Pretty soon,
> Davy (or more properly, his ghost), took over the wheel and drove
> that bus all the way to Cypress. I don't know how he learned to
> drive, but ghosts can do about anything they want to if they try
hard
> enough. We found the house of the Baby Bear and he parked out
front,
> surveying the neighborhood, which was a very nice one, indeed, for
a
> Baby Bear. Then, he turned up the walk and, just before he got to
> the front door, he thought he heard something, so he turned to the
> right and ducked under some bushes. The last I saw of him, he was
> sitting on top of the bus sighting in that long rifle, with a grin
on
> his face and a gleam in his eye. I have no idea what he had in
mind.
>
> The Ghost of IRA Boxer
>

Just
> > the other day I was thinking about Davy Crockett and wondering
what
> > was up with him, so I took a little trip over to the Alamo and
> found
> > him (more properly, his ghost), sitting there looking a little
> > dejected. He was still wearing his old buckskins and that
coonskin
> > cap which was getting a little scraggly looking, if you ask me,
and
> > he was cleaning his old Tennessee long rifle. Anyway, I asked him
> > how he had been doing and he allowed as to how he was doin'
> tol'able,
> > except that he missed his favorite pastime, which was hunting and
> > asked if I knew if there were any bears around, any old kind
would
> > do. I told him that there were very few bears left in Texas
> because
> > people like him had killed them all. He said he was sorry about
> that
> > and would like to make amends if he could. Maybe he could find a
> > bear, just any old bear, and apologize for killing so many of
them
> in
> > his lifetime. I told him that I knew of a bear out west of
> Houston,
> > but that he was just a Baby Bear. I asked him if he would like to
> > take a trip on the Texas Tour Bus and I'd show him where the cub
> > lived, if he would promise that he only wanted to apologize. He
> > brightened up at the prospect and said he'd just take me up on
it.
> > We got on board with all the other well-known Texans, a few of
whom
> > he remembered, and some he had heard of, and headed for a place
> > called Cypress, where I knew the little bear lived. Pretty soon,
> > Davy (or more properly, his ghost), took over the wheel and drove
> > that bus all the way to Cypress. I don't know how he learned to
> > drive, but ghosts can do about anything they want to if they try
> hard
> > enough. We found the house of the Baby Bear and he parked out
> front,
> > surveying the neighborhood, which was a very nice one, indeed,
for
> a
> > Baby Bear. Then, he turned up the walk and, just before he got to
> > the front door, he thought he heard something, so he turned to
the
> > right and ducked under some bushes. The last I saw of him, he was
> > sitting on top of the bus sighting in that long rifle, with a
grin
> on
> > his face and a gleam in his eye. I have no idea what he had in
> mind.
> >
> > The Ghost of IRA Boxer

Sadly, the bus does fill up, as did the TTB1, and although all 350
people on the Texas list may not have had an opportunity to add a
stamp, what can you do? The box is owned by TeamKing and it's their
call as to what they would like to do with the box once it fills up.
Maybe they'll start a TTB THREE! It's all in fun. I never got a
chance to find the second bus either, but hopefully it will make an
appearance at some of the upcoming events so I can enjoy the stamps!
(Remember, that's what we did with the original bus... shortly before
it went missing.) Puddle Splasher

Texas Tour Bus 2

From: Barefoot Lucy (barefootlucy@gmail.com) | Date: 2010-02-28 18:53:29 UTC-06:00

As we have discussed, I'll be bringing the Texas Tour Bus 2 with me to Gonzales and we will have a table set up to lay it out so folks who haven't had it can stamp it in.

If you plan to do that, you may want to bring a separate logbook for it. It's got quite a few stamps and you may not want to clutter your regular book with these stamps. Up to you though and how you manage your book...but I thought I'd throw it out there for everyone to think about.

See y'all soon!

--
Barefoot Lucy
"Not about footwear, it's about philosophy!"
